However, the liver yakitori was very large unlike any we had seen before and very very dry. Tasted a little like dogfood. The sushi was fresh and the ebi tempura was fantastic. But I wasn't sold on the yakitori. I will be coming back to try it once more and maybe update my review.< /review>< pics>

<Review>I came to Yakitori West for lunch, going to sample a selection of their Yakitori. Unfortunately, they do not serve Yakitori for lunch. That is reserved for the dinner menu only. I was a little bummed, but I decided to try their Bento Box Lunch Special. I asked the waitress to order for me (selected sashimis and mixed tempura). She said thank you for trusting me and went back into the kitchen.

The food was excellent! The fresh was very, very fresh. The tempura was lightly fried and very crispy. I really cannot say anything bad about this spot.

Looks like I need to come back for dinner. If this lunch is a predictor of what their Yakitori will be like, I will order all of it. Not a sample of each...all of it!

Kudos, Yakitori West!</Review>< pics>

< Text>
Excellent food. The steampot dish is a must eat. All yakitori items are just plain delicious.

UPDATE.  AMAZING! And they just got better with their lunch specials! No one, I say, no one is doing what they're doing right now: high quality food, authentic options, and all for $10 in a bento box. The bento special comes with a big salad, a large portion of rice, and miso soup. You can choose two items from such Japanese true staples as takoyaki (fried octopus balls with seaweed powder, bonita fish flakes, and teriyaki sauce), gyoza (best in the Tri-Valley), salmon teriyaki, Japanese croquettes (fried potato cakes) and chicken karaage (deep-fried boneless chicken to die for). Come eat for lunch and dinner (the kushiyaki grill sampler is the number one choice and best deal) and just enjoy. On weekends, for now you can avoid the lunch crowds. Good food, great pricing, and clean and friendly service. And don't forget to ask for Ramune to wash it down with all your favorite dishes!<//Text>

<Name>Jason Noell< /Name>< user>
106187409057679651083< /user>
< Text>
I am very jazzed that i discovered this small restaurant  via Yelp pumping out (based at least on what i ate today) excellent, flavorful yet subtle food.
The Left Handed Cook (and yes the chef/owner is indeed left handed) is squished into a small non-descript drive in mall next to a Mexican restaurant.
It is on Honolulu in the flats of La Crescenta which is north of Glendale and west of Montrose.
No matter where it is, Kat and are her Chef partner, Tom are pleasant, available, seemingly happy to be operating their business types. Since i was here early today and the only customer i was able to speak to them about a few subjects having to do with being left handed, the Japanese system of training Sushi chefs, etc.
One of the things i enjoy/crave really is to establish a personal but of course only business relationship with business owners so as to attempt to get at the heart and soul of a business. Why do this when there are so many pitfalls that can trip you up in the process?
Well all of that being said, i ordered a couple of things:
Rice Rice Baby
Side order of Fries
The menu board lists the Rice Rice Baby with this ingredient statement: Beef Brisket, Bacon, Kimchi, fried rice, pickled jalapeno, Furikake. Whew!
The first thing that occurred to me is: with so many listed ingredients will it all just be a mish mash of conflicting flavors?
The only thing that i could not taste was the kimchi. But overall, this product Pops with flavor: slow cooked, beefy brisket, a good dose of pickled jalapeno, smoky bacon all topped by a creamy poached egg and spinkled with Furikake ( a japanese seasoning of dried fish, sesame seeds, chopped seaweed, sugar, salt.) and perfectly cooked brown rice.
The Rice Rice Baby is not at all salty (particularly with so many salt forward ingredients) but properly seasoned with salt. It is an unctuously delicious item. A note: Tom please think about adding a "double the brisket for X dollars." I craved more meat.
Fries:
i ordered a side of Fries because the photos posted here gave me a jones for them. And i was correct. These are hand sliced, slightly sweet fries: more like what we used to call Steak Fries. A success for sure. The high level of attention to detail is often more revealingly  apparent with the simplicity of the preparation of these fries than it is in the more complex items. Meaning: if you can make the simple things like fried potatoes special: you will  also appreciably extend that attention to detail to the more complex products.
Yes i realize that i seem to be bubbling over with enthusiasm for The Left Handed Cook: it is because i am. I can't wait to bring my family here so that we can order every thing on their menu.</Text>

<user_name>M. A. Grisso</user_name><UserId.>109450308737686183784<//UserId.>< text>
** AVOID ONLINE ORDERING AND/OR DELIVERY **

Marsa Lounge took 2 hours (from the time I submitted my order) to deliver my food. I ordered around 3:40 PM, a time that one can safely assume is NOT busy for restaurants (which google analytics supports in showing this sparsely frequented time as "usually not busy"), and was told by their online ordering system that I could expect delivery "around 4:30 PM Today". After 45 minutes passed the delivery ETA, I called the restaurant to ask about my order that was nearly an hour late. All I was told was "sorry, the delivery guy already left". I still didn't receive my order until around 5:40 PM, about 2 hours after I submitted the order.

This is absurd because the restaurant is about an 11 minute drive (a little over 3 miles) from the address ordered from. How can it possibly take 2 hours to prepare and deliver a 3 item order? It would've been faster to take the bus there, order take out, and then take the bus back. Or, rather, it would've been faster and cheaper to go to the grocery store and cook myself something to eat.

Needless to say, the food was barely warm when it arrived, which checks out as it was likely sitting out for a great deal of time before it was actually out in transit for delivery.

Marsa Lounge should consider either revamping their online order & delivery process to accurately represent delivery ETAs or discontinue offering delivery & online ordering altogether until they are equipped to professionally handle these.

As for the food itself, it wasn't bad. I had not eaten in almost 12 hours so pretty much anything tastes good at that point. The only reason I gave 2 stars instead of 1 was because the food was edible and somewhat tasty.

My only other complaint is that the hummus is overpriced, as it is at many restaurants, seeing as it's so much cheaper to make at home. Anyone with a food processor and a brain could make homemade hummus.<//text>

<Text>Sunny's Restaurant is one of the last TRULY GREAT Family Style, American Restaurants, that I know of in this area. I have been eating at Sunny's for (at least) 30 years (on & off) now. Over the years, I've had the pleasure not only of trying everything on the menu, at one time or another, but also of getting to know the Terrific service staff. In addition to the Waiters/Waitresses, it's been my honor to become good friends with the owners/founders of Sunny's, Andy & Cindy, as well as their kids (roughly my age) Summer & Shadow. Now for the Good Stuff‚Ñ¢:
THE FOOD-
All of the food served at Sunny's is prepared the Old-Fashioned way. For example, if you order a turkey sandwich, it's prepared with freshly (in-house) roasted turkey, carved straight off the bird. This style of fresh made food (never canned or frozen), carries through to all the dishes they make. I LOVE the Daily Specials, because they are usually -$2 Off the full menu price. 1569296438284</Date>
< UserId.>
102477604135821589862</UserId.>
<Pics>None</Pics><review>Room was hot, but food was good</review><Response>None</Response></record></dataset><record>
<rating>4<//rating><userid>107030750642176652929< /userid><GmapID>0x80dd2133e97ba601:0x4b7126722b2b9882</GmapID><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< text>
I eat here regularly and really enjoy this place. I've enjoyed Sunny's for about 10 years. Note-if you're looking for some hipster, fusion, happening place then this probably isn't for you. Sunny's is old school, diner, American food. The prices are reasonable and the food good, basic fare. Their portions are generous and the variety seems wide.

They have wonderful, hearty breakfasts and I have enjoyed everything I've ordered over the years although I'm partial to the Country Breakfast. They have daily dinner specials that are a good deal and seasonal specials, all of which are good deals and tasty food.

As for the staff, everyone I've encountered over the years has taken reasonably good care of us and, because I've eaten there over such a long period of time, they will recognize me and extend a warm welcome.

I agree that this is probably a place favored by a slightly older crowd and that's just fine with me. There are also families and a variety of ages that I've seen there too. I don't think I've seen any hipsters, though, so maybe not the place to go if you're looking for someplace trendy and hip.

Maybe one of the reasons for a preponderance of negative reviews on Google is the fact that the older people, and there are a bunch, who eat there aren't as familiar with social media, online review sites, and the importance of online reviews. They just now that they enjoy Sunny's and are probably okay that not everyone is as into the Sunny's experience like they are.

As for the decor, yeah, they could probably do with an update or refresh; however, as we all know, when that happens the ambiance, and some would say "charm" of the place would change, as well as the prices, undoubtedly. However, they entire center where Sunny's is located has undergone an exterior remodel/modernization that, as of this review, is nearly complete. Consequently, the outside is looking much cleaner and more modern but the interior is mostly unchanged.

I understand that people's experiences can vary widely in any service industry but I would encourage anyone who's thinking about eating at Sunny's to give it a try and come with an open mind. Don't let the haters discourage you; who knows, maybe you'll find the charm in this place as I have done. In a way, it's kind of like going back in time to when you could go to a neighborhood diner and just eat good food with friends.

Enjoy!<//text>

<userid>106031388151885654404< /userid><time>1515666438205< /time><GmapID>0x80dd2133e97ba601:0x4b7126722b2b9882<//GmapID><name>Kai Force< /name>< Text>
This review is a little bit late in coming. The first time I walked in to Sunny's, I was about 11yo. In April, I'll be 43. OK, OK, A LOT LATE IN COMING. I thinks that it's difficult to right a fair review when you know people forever, but I'm gonna try.
1) The Food: This isn't the type of restaurant that you see every day (especially anymore). I'll explain. If you order a turkey sandwich, for example, they carve fresh turkey from the birds that they Freshly Roasted that day. Their soups are not "frozen in a bag" they a Freshly crafted by their talented kitchen staff.
This is how all restaurants used to be, or so I've been told.
2)The People: I'll try to be brief. The Zervos family has been in the restaurant business for an incredibly long time. Andy, the patriarch has run numerous restaurants in Orange County, even another Sunnys which used to be in South H.B. The Zervos family and their staff are more than mere restaurateurs. They are the people who remember your name. The ones who ask about family members, when they haven't seen them in too long. They are the people who sent home an order of soup, when they heard I was sick.
To sum it up, Andy, Cindy, their Children, and staff, are like family. It's like eating at your favorite aunt's house. It's being surrounded by people who care, and people you care about in return.
3)The Restaurant: Sunny's just completed a HUGE exterior renovation, and it couldn't look better outside. Haven't seen any noticeable changes inside yet, but I'm Certain that it is only a matter of time before they get to that also. I will be very honest, the interior is significantly dated in appearance. I know that can be a turn off to some people who are looking for the newest hippest spots. This isn't new or hip. It's Classic, a bit dated, and the food, service, and staff, are the BEST that you are likely to find, ANYWHERE in Orange County.< /Text>
